{
 "cells": [
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "# Influence of the grid for continuum states\n",
    "\n",
    "Last but not least, the grid is a very important parameter when it comes to find the eigenstates of a Hamiltonian matrix. Two parameters characterize a 1D grid: the grid spacing (the distance between two grid points) and the grid extension (the range spanned by the $x$-axis). Let us find out how these parameters influence the continuum and bound states found numerically."
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "## Initialization"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "### Import some modules and classes"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 1,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "from siegpy import (Hamiltonian, SWPotential, UniformCoordMap,\n",
    "                    SWPBasisSet)\n",
    "import numpy as np\n",
    "from copy import deepcopy"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "### Define a potential"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 2,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "siegerts = SWPBasisSet.from_file(\"siegerts.dat\")\n",
    "pot = siegerts.potential"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "## Influence of the grid step\n",
    "\n",
    "Having two parameters to consider, we'll vary one while keeping the other constant. Let us begin with the grid step. The grid extension being constant, this amounts to using different number of grid points."
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "### Define the same potential with multiple grid steps"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 3,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [
    {
     "name": "stdout",
     "output_type": "stream",
     "text": [
      "npts_list: [51, 101, 201, 401, 801]\n",
      "grid spacings: [0.29999999999999982, 0.15000000000000036, 0.075000000000000178, 0.037499999999999645, 0.018749999999999822]\n"
     ]
    }
   ],
   "source": [
    "# Set the grid extension\n",
    "xmax = 7.5\n",
    "# Set the various grids\n",
    "factors = [1, 2, 4, 8, 16]\n",
    "npts_list = [f*50 + 1 for f in factors]\n",
    "print('npts_list:', npts_list)\n",
    "xgrids = [np.linspace(-xmax, xmax, npts) for npts in npts_list]\n",
    "# List the grid steps\n",
    "hx_list = [g[1]-g[0] for g in xgrids]\n",
    "print(\"grid spacings:\", hx_list)\n",
    "# Discretize the potential over the multiple grid steps\n",
    "pots = []\n",
    "for xgrid in xgrids:\n",
    "    pots.append(deepcopy(pot))\n",
    "    pots[-1].grid = xgrid"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "### Define the coordinate mapping\n",
    "\n",
    "The same coordinate mapping will be used throughout this notebook."
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 4,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "theta = 0.0\n",
    "cm = UniformCoordMap(theta)"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "### Define the Hamiltonians"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 5,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "hams_hx = [Hamiltonian(pot, cm) for pot in pots]"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "### Solve the Hamiltonians"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 6,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "basissets_hx = [ham.solve() for ham in hams_hx]"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "### Compare the spectra\n",
    "\n",
    "As usual, the easiest way is to plot the energies of the eigenstates and their virial values:"
   ]

   "source": [
    "## Influence of the grid extension\n",
    "\n",
    "Let us now review how the grid extension influences the eigenstates."
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "### Define the same potential with multiple grid extensions"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 11,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [
    {
     "name": "stdout",
     "output_type": "stream",
     "text": [
      "xmax_list: [3.75, 7.5, 11.25, 15.0, 18.75]\n",
      "npts_list: [201, 401, 601, 801, 1001]\n"
     ]
    }
   ],
   "source": [
    "# Set the grid spacing\n",
    "hx = 0.0375\n",
    "# Set the various grids via the grid extension\n",
    "factors = range(1, 6)\n",
    "xmax_list = [f*100*hx for f in factors]\n",
    "print('xmax_list:', xmax_list)\n",
    "xgrids = [np.arange(-xmax, xmax+hx/2, hx) for xmax in xmax_list]\n",
    "# List the number of points\n",
    "npts_list = [len(g) for g in xgrids]\n",
    "print('npts_list:', npts_list)\n",
    "# Discretize the potential over the multiple grid steps\n",
    "pots = []\n",
    "for xgrid in xgrids:\n",
    "    pots.append(deepcopy(pot))\n",
    "    pots[-1].grid = xgrid"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "### Define the Hamiltonians"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 12,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "# The same uniform coordinate mapping is used\n",
    "hams_xmax = [Hamiltonian(pot, cm) for pot in pots]"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "### Solve the Hamiltonians"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "code",
   "execution_count": 13,
   "metadata": {},
   "outputs": [],
   "source": [
    "basissets_xmax = [ham.solve() for ham in hams_xmax]"
   ]
  },

   "source": [
    "These plots show that the spectrum in this range is largely modified by the grid extension: there is a convergence of the bound states, but not of the continuum states. The latter fact is known as the continuum collapse, and is related to the confinement (*i.e.*, it is as if the 1D square-well potential was embedded inside a larger, infinite square well potential). It causes trouble whenever one is interested in having a finer sampling of the high energy spectrum of continuum states, because using a larger grid extension causes an accumulation above the threshold energy (here 0). This is actually one motivation for using the Siegert states instead of continuum states: thanks to the smooth exterior complex scaling, there is no need to largely increase the grid extension, because then the resonant states resemble bound states. This will be presented in the next notebook.\n",
    "\n",
    "The bound states being normalizable, then can however easily converge with respect to the grid extension: it has to be large enough to accomodate for the exponential tails of the highest energy bound states.\n",
    "\n",
    "These facts are evidenced by the next cells:"
   ]

    "    print(\"Continuum state n° {}:\".format(i+1))\n",

    "        msg = \"xmax = {:.2f}; E = {:.4e}\".format(xmax_list[j], basis.continuum[i].energy.real)\n",
    "        show_plots = False  # Set to True to show plots instead\n",
    "        if show_plots:\n",
    "            basis.continuum[i].plot(title=msg)\n",
    "        else:\n",
    "            print(msg)"
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "The continuum collapse is clearly evidenced here: the energy of the $n$-th continuum state decreases when the grid extension increases. By plotting the wavefunctions of these states, one could see that the wavefunctions of these states are not always related to eachother."
   ]
  },
  {
   "cell_type": "markdown",
   "metadata": {},
   "source": [
    "## Conclusion\n",
    "\n",
    "The two grid step and the grid extension are the two parameters to consider to reach a convergence of the numerical eigenstates (at least when using grids where the points are not evenly distributed). They have two distincts influence on the obtained spectra:\n",
    "\n",
    "- Decreasing the grid step allows for states of better quality (*i.e.*, of lower virial), and the bound and continuum states converge to a given value, even though the convergence is rather slow (*e.g.*, it may require a large number of grid points). It also allows to define continuum states of higher energy.\n",
    "\n",
    "- Increasing the grid extension allows for a convergence of the bound states only (the grid extension must be large enough for their exponential tail to vanish), but not for the continuum states, where an accumulation of states above the zero energy is observed (known as the continuum collapse) while leaving the range of energies and virial values unchanged. This means that there is no need to increase the grid extension if the bound states are converged with respect to this parameter and if the discretization of the continuum states allows to reach high enough energies with a sufficient precision."
   ]
  }
